<p><b>Leeds railway station</b> (also known as <b>Leeds City railway station</b>)<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> is the mainline railway station serving the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_city_centre" title="Leeds city centre">city centre</a> of <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> in West Yorkshire, England. It is the third-busiest railway station in the UK outside London (as of 2018).<sup id="cite_ref-Commercial_information_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commercial_information-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> It is located on New Station Street to the south of <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Square" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds City Square">City Square</a>, at the bottom of Park Row, behind the landmark <a href="/wiki/Queens_Hotel_(Leeds)" class="mw-redirect" title="Queens Hotel (Leeds)">Queens Hotel</a>. It is one of 20 stations managed by <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Commercial_information_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commercial_information-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Leeds is an important hub on the British rail network. The station is the terminus of the Leeds branch of the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a> (on which London North Eastern Railway provides high speed inter-city services to London every half hour from the station) and is an important stop on the <a href="/wiki/Cross_Country_Route" title="Cross Country Route">Cross Country Route</a> between <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/English_Midlands" class="mw-redirect" title="English Midlands">Midlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_West_England" title="South West England">South West England</a> connecting to major cities such as <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derby" title="Derby">Derby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nottingham" title="Nottingham">Nottingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Berkshire" title="Reading, Berkshire">Reading</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Penzance" title="Penzance">Penzance</a>. There are also regular inter-city services to major destinations throughout <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">Northern England</a> including <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>. It is also the terminus for trains running on the scenic <a href="/wiki/Settle-Carlisle_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Settle-Carlisle Railway">Settle to Carlisle Line</a>. Future expansion will link the station to the proposed High Speed 2 (<a href="/wiki/HS2" class="mw-redirect" title="HS2">HS2</a>) network.
</p><p>Leeds is a major hub for local and regional destinations across <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a> such as to <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scarborough,_North_Yorkshire" title="Scarborough, North Yorkshire">Scarborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doncaster" title="Doncaster">Doncaster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>. The station lies at the heart of the <a href="/wiki/MetroTrain" class="mw-redirect" title="MetroTrain">Metro</a> <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Commuter rail in the United Kingdom">commuter network</a> for <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a> providing services to <a href="/wiki/Bradford" title="Bradford">Bradford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wakefield" title="Wakefield">Wakefield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dewsbury" title="Dewsbury">Dewsbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield" title="Huddersfield">Huddersfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_West_Yorkshire" title="Halifax, West Yorkshire">Halifax</a>.
</p><p>With over 31 million passenger entries and exits between April 2017 and March 2018, Leeds is the busiest railway station in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">North of England</a> and the third-busiest railway station in the United Kingdom outside London, after <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_New_Street_railway_station" title="Birmingham New Street railway station">Birmingham New Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Glasgow Central</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Description">Description</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Description">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_City_railway_station_concourse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Leeds_City_railway_station_concourse.jpg/220px-Leeds_City_railway_station_concourse.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Leeds_City_railway_station_concourse.jpg/330px-Leeds_City_railway_station_concourse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Leeds_City_railway_station_concourse.jpg/440px-Leeds_City_railway_station_concourse.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_City_railway_station_concourse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The North Concourse (Wellington Quarter) by <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Hamlyn" title="William Henry Hamlyn">William Henry Hamlyn</a> dating from 1937/38 – The shops on the right were previously platform entrances</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_station_letters.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Leeds_station_letters.jpg/220px-Leeds_station_letters.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Leeds_station_letters.jpg/330px-Leeds_station_letters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Leeds_station_letters.jpg/440px-Leeds_station_letters.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_station_letters.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 6-foot high 'LEEDS' letters inside the main entrance to the station</div></div></div>
<p>The railway station is situated on a hill falling from the south of the city to the <a href="/wiki/River_Aire" title="River Aire">River Aire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_and_Liverpool_Canal" title="Leeds and Liverpool Canal">Leeds and Liverpool Canal</a> basin. Much of it is supported on <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">Victorian</a> brick-vaulted arches situated just off Neville Street which contain a centre consisting of cafés, restaurants, shops and exhibition spaces called <a href="/wiki/Granary_Wharf" title="Granary Wharf">Granary Wharf</a>, known locally as the Dark Arches.
</p><p>The railway station has 17 platforms, making it the largest by number of platforms in England outside London. There are 11 terminus and six through platforms. Most platforms are subdivided into up to four sections, i.e. 1a, 1b, 1c etc. All together including the numbers, there are 47 platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Retail facilities in the station include coffee shops, fast food outlets, a bar, newsagents, chemists, and supermarkets. A <a href="/wiki/British_Transport_Police" title="British Transport Police">British Transport Police</a> station on New Station Street houses officers who police the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a> railway stations.
</p><p>Leeds railway station retained manned ticket barriers through the 1990s until 2008 when they were replaced by automatic barriers by <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> to reduce congestion around the barriers at peak times.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Platforms</dt></dl>
<p>Platform usage varies depending on operational circumstances but is generally:
</p>
<ul><li>1–5 – <a href="/wiki/Bay_platform" title="Bay platform">Bay platforms</a> mostly used by <a href="/wiki/MetroTrain" class="mw-redirect" title="MetroTrain">MetroTrain</a> services operated by <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a>, towards <a href="/wiki/Harrogate_railway_station" title="Harrogate railway station">Harrogate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilkley_railway_station" title="Ilkley railway station">Ilkley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Forster_Square_railway_station" title="Bradford Forster Square railway station">Bradford Forster Square</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skipton_railway_station" title="Skipton railway station">Skipton</a>.</li>
<li>6, 8 – 6 is a Bay Platform used for terminating <a href="/wiki/London_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London North Eastern Railway">London North Eastern Railway</a> services from London, 8 is a through platform used for London North Eastern Railway services which both terminate and continue onward to Bradford, Harrogate and Skipton, as well as the early morning LNER departure to Aberdeen.</li>
<li>8, 9, 11, 12, 15, 16 – through platforms. CrossCountry services heading north to York and beyond depart from Platforms 8, 9 or 11; services heading south use platform 12. Platforms 15 and 16 are used by north/east and south/westbound TransPennine Express services to Hull, Newcastle, York, Scarborough and Middlesbrough and Huddersfield, Manchester Airport and Liverpool Lime Street.</li>
<li>7, 14 – Bay platforms used for local Northern services running north/east from Leeds.</li>
<li>10, 13, 17 – Bay platforms used for local and regional services running south/west to Manchester Victoria and Huddersfield, alongside southbound services towards Wakefield, Barnsley, Meadowhall, Sheffield and Nottingham.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_links">Transport links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Transport links">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_City_(6282693111).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Leeds_City_%286282693111%29.jpg/220px-Leeds_City_%286282693111%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Leeds_City_%286282693111%29.jpg/330px-Leeds_City_%286282693111%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Leeds_City_%286282693111%29.jpg/440px-Leeds_City_%286282693111%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4592" data-file-height="3056" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_City_(6282693111).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Western Entrance into the railway station.</div></div></div>
<p>Leeds Interchange, located at the New Station Street exit, provides onward transport connections from the station. There are five bus stands serving Arriva, First and Yorkshire Tiger routes 4, 5, 16, 16A, 19, 19A, 40, 85, 87, 90, 757, 870 and DalesBus services. A 24-hour taxi rank also operates at the interchange.
</p><p>Further bus stops are located on Neville Street below the railway station, as well as around City Square outside the railway station. Infirmary Street and Boar Lane Bus Points are a short walk for more bus connections.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cycle_hub">Cycle hub</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cycle hub">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Leeds Interchange hosts one of the UK's first cycle hubs that allows a number of cycling services including repair, storage and rental. The facility opened in summer 2010 and is designed to encourage visitors and commuters into Leeds to continue their journey from the railway station by bike.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Its design is based on the Dutch cyclepoint concept.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_railway_stations">Past railway stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Past railway stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Under_Leeds_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Under_Leeds_station.jpg/220px-Under_Leeds_station.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Under_Leeds_station.jpg/330px-Under_Leeds_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Under_Leeds_station.jpg/440px-Under_Leeds_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Under_Leeds_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Neville Street passes under the railway station</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_RJD_40.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Leeds_RJD_40.jpg/220px-Leeds_RJD_40.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Leeds_RJD_40.jpg/330px-Leeds_RJD_40.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Leeds_RJD_40.jpg/440px-Leeds_RJD_40.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2861" data-file-height="1890" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_RJD_40.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Railway lines in central Leeds in 1913</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_Station_South.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Leeds_Station_South.jpg/220px-Leeds_Station_South.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Leeds_Station_South.jpg/330px-Leeds_Station_South.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Leeds_Station_South.jpg/440px-Leeds_Station_South.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_Station_South.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The river Aire and Southern station entrance</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_City_Station_1974.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Leeds_City_Station_1974.jpg/220px-Leeds_City_Station_1974.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Leeds_City_Station_1974.jpg/330px-Leeds_City_Station_1974.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Leeds_City_Station_1974.jpg/440px-Leeds_City_Station_1974.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="513" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_City_Station_1974.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The railway station seen in 1974</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LEEDSCITYTROLLEY.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/87/LEEDSCITYTROLLEY.jpg/220px-LEEDSCITYTROLLEY.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/87/LEEDSCITYTROLLEY.jpg/330px-LEEDSCITYTROLLEY.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/87/LEEDSCITYTROLLEY.jpg/440px-LEEDSCITYTROLLEY.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LEEDSCITYTROLLEY.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A trolley point showing the historical name of 'Leeds City' after the 2002 rebuilding</div></div></div>
<p>The railways arrived in Leeds in 1834 when the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_and_Selby_Railway" title="Leeds and Selby Railway">Leeds and Selby Railway</a> (which became part of the <a href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Railway_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="North Eastern Railway (UK)">North Eastern Railway</a>) opened its line. It had a terminus at <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Marsh_Lane_railway_station" title="Leeds Marsh Lane railway station">Marsh Lane</a> east of the city centre. In 1840, the <a href="/wiki/North_Midland_Railway" title="North Midland Railway">North Midland Railway</a> (a constituent of the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Railway" title="Midland Railway">Midland Railway</a>) constructed its line from <a href="/wiki/Derby" title="Derby">Derby</a> via <a href="/wiki/Rotherham" title="Rotherham">Rotherham</a> to a terminus at <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Hunslet_Lane_railway_station" title="Leeds Hunslet Lane railway station">Hunslet Lane</a> to the south. It was extended to a more centrally located terminus at Wellington Street in 1846, known as <i>Wellington Station</i>.
</p><p>Another railway station, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Central_railway_station" title="Leeds Central railway station"><i>Leeds Central</i></a> (on Wellington Street), was opened in 1854 by the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_and_Leeds_Railway" title="Manchester and Leeds Railway">Manchester and Leeds Railway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/London_and_North_Western_Railway" title="London and North Western Railway">London and North Western Railway</a>, or LNWR. The railway station became owned jointly by the LNWR and the North Eastern Railway, but other companies had powers to run trains there, including the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Railway_(Great_Britain)" title="Great Northern Railway (Great Britain)">Great Northern Railway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lancashire_and_Yorkshire_Railway" title="Lancashire and Yorkshire Railway">Lancashire and Yorkshire Railway</a>.
</p><p>In 1869 <i>New Station</i> opened as a joint enterprise by the LNWR and the North Eastern Railway. It connected the former Leeds and Selby Railway Line to the east with the LNWR lines to the west. A mile-long connection was built, carried entirely on viaducts and bridges. New Station was built partially on a bridge over the River Aire adjacent to Wellington railway station.
</p><p>The map to the right shows the variety of different railway lines in Leeds in 1913.
Following the <a href="/wiki/Railways_Act_1921" title="Railways Act 1921">1921 Railways Act</a>, when railways in Great Britain were grouped into four companies, New Station was jointly operated by the <a href="/wiki/London,_Midland_and_Scottish_Railway" title="London, Midland and Scottish Railway">London, Midland and Scottish Railway</a> (LMS) and the <a href="/wiki/London_and_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London and North Eastern Railway">London and North Eastern Railway</a> (LNER).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1938_rebuilding">1938 rebuilding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1938 rebuilding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_City_South_Station_geograph-2192440.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Leeds_City_South_Station_geograph-2192440.jpg/220px-Leeds_City_South_Station_geograph-2192440.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Leeds_City_South_Station_geograph-2192440.jpg/330px-Leeds_City_South_Station_geograph-2192440.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Leeds_City_South_Station_geograph-2192440.jpg/440px-Leeds_City_South_Station_geograph-2192440.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="566" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_City_South_Station_geograph-2192440.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leeds City South Station: west end, in 1961</div></div></div>
<p>The first rationalisation occurred in 1938, when two railway stations (New and Wellington) were combined to form <i>Leeds City Station</i>, opening on 2 May that year. This was designed by LMS architect <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Hamlyn" title="William Henry Hamlyn">William Henry Hamlyn</a>. The third railway station, Leeds Central, was unaffected by the change. Part of Wellington railway station later became a parcels depot. The north concourse and the Queens Hotel were built at this time.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leeds_Blitz">Leeds Blitz</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Leeds Blitz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Blitz" title="Leeds Blitz">Leeds Blitz</a></div>
<p>In 1939, the <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> launched attacks in England with one taking place in <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armley" title="Armley">Armley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beeston,_Leeds" title="Beeston, Leeds">Beeston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bramley,_West_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Bramley, West Yorkshire">Bramley</a>. Leeds New Station was one of the primary targets along with the Town Hall, Kirkgate Markets, the Central Post office, the Quarry Hill flats, Hotel Metropole and part of the Inner Ring Road. The station was bombed with unknown casualty numbers, the station was rebuilt however.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1962_British_Railways_House">1962 British Railways House</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1962 British Railways House">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/City_House" title="City House">City House</a></div>
<p>In 1962 British Railways House, now City House, was added to the railway station. It was designed by architect <a href="/wiki/John_Poulson" title="John Poulson">John Poulson</a> providing British Railways with administrative buildings. The building became dated and hard to let before refurbishment in 2009. The building was lambasted in 1967 by poet <a href="/wiki/John_Betjeman" title="John Betjeman">John Betjeman</a> who said it blocked all the light out of <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Square" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds City Square">City Square</a>, and was a testament to money with no architectural merit. In 2010 the building was bought by property company Bruntwood which is (as of 2017) redeveloping it to provide serviced offices, with a new look to the façade.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1967_rebuilding">1967 rebuilding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1967 rebuilding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1967 further remodelling of the site took place and trains using Central Railway Station were diverted into the City Railway Station which became the main railway station serving the city. Central Railway Station was closed and has been demolished. The viaduct leading to Central Railway Station is one of many disused viaducts near Leeds Railway Station.  Engineering work included replacing 100-year-old bridges over the Leeds and Liverpool Canal, the construction of the south concourse &amp; an overall roof, along with major platform and track layout alterations and the commissioning of a new power signal box to control the railway station area.
</p><p>At the time of this rebuilding, the railway station was served by 500 trains on a typical day, with 2.75&#160;million passenger journeys a year. Wellington (or City North) became entirely devoted to parcels traffic at this time with the track layout extensively changed. The remaining Midland line trains which previously used City North station were diverted into the City South station, the former LNWR/NER 'New' station, and called simply Leeds from this time.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2002_rebuilding">2002 rebuilding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2002 rebuilding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Platforms_3-5_at_Leeds_City_railway_station_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Platforms_3-5_at_Leeds_City_railway_station_01.jpg/220px-Platforms_3-5_at_Leeds_City_railway_station_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Platforms_3-5_at_Leeds_City_railway_station_01.jpg/330px-Platforms_3-5_at_Leeds_City_railway_station_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Platforms_3-5_at_Leeds_City_railway_station_01.jpg/440px-Platforms_3-5_at_Leeds_City_railway_station_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Platforms_3-5_at_Leeds_City_railway_station_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Platforms three to five</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Transpennine_train_at_Leeds_(geograph_4704285).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Transpennine_train_at_Leeds_%28geograph_4704285%29.jpg/220px-Transpennine_train_at_Leeds_%28geograph_4704285%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Transpennine_train_at_Leeds_%28geograph_4704285%29.jpg/330px-Transpennine_train_at_Leeds_%28geograph_4704285%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Transpennine_train_at_Leeds_%28geograph_4704285%29.jpg/440px-Transpennine_train_at_Leeds_%28geograph_4704285%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Transpennine_train_at_Leeds_(geograph_4704285).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Outer platforms</div></div></div>
<p>By the 1990s, the railway station's capacity was exceeded on a daily basis, and the 1967 design was deemed inadequate. Between 1999 and 2002, a major rebuilding project took place, branded as <i>Leeds 1st</i>. This project saw the construction of additional approach tracks at the western end of the railway station, improving efficiency by separating trains travelling to or from different destinations and preventing them from having to cross each other's routes. The railway station was expanded from 12 to 17 platforms, with the construction of new platforms on the south side, and reopening of the disused parcels depot to passengers on the north side.
</p><p>The majority of the track, points and signals were also replaced and the 1967 power box closed – control being handed over to the signalling centre at <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a>.  The most visible change to passengers, however, was the replacement of the 1967 metal canopy with a new glass roof, considerably increasing the amount of daylight on the platforms. A new footbridge was also provided, replacing the previous underpass. Ancillary improvements included a new multi-storey car park and railway station entrance, refurbishing the North Concourse and expanding retail facilities.
</p><p>A small temporary railway station called <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Whitehall_railway_station" title="Leeds Whitehall railway station">Leeds Whitehall</a> was provided to handle some services while the railway station was being remodelled. This has now been demolished.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_work">2008 work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2008 work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2008 automated ticket gates were installed in place of the human-controlled ticket checking, to speed up the passage of passengers. When the gates came into operation at the end of October 2008 they suffered from several faults including accepting expired tickets.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> An oversight on the part of Northern also meant that the gates were not compatible with West Yorkshire Metro Cards.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_entrance">Southern entrance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Southern entrance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A £17.3&#160;million southern entrance to allow for easier access from the south completed on 3 January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-lssestart_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lssestart-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>  It widens the railway station's western footbridge and provide escalators, stairs and lifts to a partial deck over the River Aire in an iconic structure. The deck provides access to either side of the river for passengers to access Granary Wharf and Little Neville Street or <a href="/wiki/Holbeck" title="Holbeck">Holbeck</a>. It contains extra ticket vending machines and cycle storage. Around 20%<sup id="cite_ref-lssestart_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lssestart-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> of passengers are expected to use the new entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>On 23 July 1993, a passenger train ran into the rear of another occupying a platform. Twenty-one people were injured; one seriously.<sup id="cite_ref-Plymouth_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plymouth-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On 17 April 1997 a small bomb planted by the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">Provisional Irish Republican Army</a> exploded at a relay cabinet near the station, causing the city centre's closure for six hours.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Leeds City railway station is the third-busiest railway station outside London in England;<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> being a very busy railway station, expansion is needed. Passenger numbers at Leeds are expected to surge by 63% by 2029, meaning further expansion is necessary.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_Remodelling">Future Remodelling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Future Remodelling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 2017, it was proposed that the station could be remodelled for the proposed HS2 scheme. The proposal includes new platforms on the northside of Leeds as well as HS2 services running into the existing east-west platforms as well as the proposed terminal platforms allowing links to proposed 'Northern Powerhouse Rail'.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In November 2017, details were released about how the station might look.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion">Expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Plans are being drawn up to expand the railway station's capacity with new lines and platforms alongside platform one in the Riverside Car Park on the site of the original Leeds Wellington railway station to cater for predicted growth. Also <a href="/wiki/Metro_(West_Yorkshire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Metro (West Yorkshire)">Metro</a> announced plans to replace platforms 1A, 1B and 1C with three separate platforms using the car park next to the platform 1's. This would increase platform numbers from 17 to 19.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_concourse">South concourse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: South concourse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Network Rail plans to improve the south concourse by opening up the skylights to allow in natural light. The first phase of works will aim to reduce congestion. Consideration will be given to a mezzanine level for retail units. Network Rail has said that it "is looking at the feasibility of the provision of a new roof to the concourse. The latter scheme is one that will be taken forward in conjunction with Bruntwood" in connection with the redevelopment of City House.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_service">Future service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Future service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In June 2014, <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> accepted <a href="/wiki/Alliance_Rail" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance Rail">Alliance Rail</a> t/a Great North Western Railway Company (GNWR) to operate services between <a href="/wiki/London_Euston" class="mw-redirect" title="London Euston">London Euston</a> and Leeds via <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Bank_Quay_railway_station" title="Warrington Bank Quay railway station">Warrington Bank Quay</a> and Huddersfield with six services per day in both directions. The services were proposed to start in 2017 using Pendolino trains.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
However, in January 2015 the proposed services were rejected.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/London_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London North Eastern Railway">London North Eastern Railway</a> plan to operate direct services between <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London King's Cross</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_railway_station" title="Huddersfield railway station">Huddersfield</a> via Leeds from 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As part of the new <a href="/wiki/Arriva_Rail_North" class="mw-redirect" title="Arriva Rail North">Arriva Rail North</a> franchise, from May 2019 there will be a new hourly service to <a href="/wiki/Chester_railway_station" title="Chester railway station">Chester</a>, calling at <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Interchange" title="Bradford Interchange">Bradford Interchange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Victoria railway station">Manchester Victoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Bank_Quay_railway_station" title="Warrington Bank Quay railway station">Warrington Bank Quay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
Originally planned for December 2017<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> the introduction has been delayed for operational reasons.  New services to <a href="/wiki/Bridlington_railway_station" title="Bridlington railway station">Bridlington</a> via Hull will also be introduced and those to Nottingham will be re-routed via Wakefield Westgate rather than via Barnsley (saving 20+ minutes' journey time) and extended to/from Bradford Interchange. There will also be new direct services to Lincoln via Barnsley and Worksop.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>  These new routes will be marketed under the "Northern Connect" brand and use new <a href="/wiki/Diesel_multiple_units" class="mw-redirect" title="Diesel multiple units">DMUs</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="HS2_platforms">HS2 platforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: HS2 platforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_station_proposed_HS2_platforms.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Leeds_station_proposed_HS2_platforms.png/220px-Leeds_station_proposed_HS2_platforms.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Leeds_station_proposed_HS2_platforms.png/330px-Leeds_station_proposed_HS2_platforms.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Leeds_station_proposed_HS2_platforms.png/440px-Leeds_station_proposed_HS2_platforms.png 2x" data-file-width="817" data-file-height="724" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_station_proposed_HS2_platforms.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A graphical mockup showing how new HS2 platforms (blue) will be joined to the existing Leeds station platforms (pink).</div></div></div>
<p>The original plans for <a href="/wiki/HS2" class="mw-redirect" title="HS2">HS2</a> proposed a separate new station in Leeds to the south of the River Aire at <a href="/wiki/Leeds_New_Lane_railway_station" title="Leeds New Lane railway station">New Lane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> However, a later review in November 2015 instead recommends that HS2 platforms be added to the existing station.<sup id="cite_ref-Yorkshire_Hub_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yorkshire_Hub-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> These would attach to the southern part of the existing station building, and span the river in a North-South alignment to create a 'T' shape.
</p><p>Whilst not directly linking the rail lines, it will allow a common concourse for easy interchange between high speed and classic rail services.  These plans were approved by the Government in November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The railway station is served by train operators, <a href="/wiki/London_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London North Eastern Railway">London North Eastern Railway</a>, <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a>, <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a>. It is also the hub of the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Passenger_Transport_Executive#Rail_(MetroTrain)" class="mw-redirect" title="West Yorkshire Passenger Transport Executive">MetroTrain</a> network in <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a>, being the terminus of the following lines:
</p>
<ul><li>The Leeds branch of the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a> to London King's Cross</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">Midland Main Line</a> to London St Pancras</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Airedale_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Airedale Line">Airedale Line</a> to Keighley/Skipton/Heysham Port/Morcambe/Carlisle</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caldervale_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Caldervale Line">Caldervale Line</a> to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Oxford_Road_railway_station" title="Manchester Oxford Road railway station">Manchester Oxford Road</a> /Blackpool North/Huddersfield</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hallam_Line" title="Hallam Line">Hallam Line</a> to Castleford/Wakefield/Barnsley/Sheffield</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harrogate_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Harrogate Line">Harrogate Line</a> to Harrogate/Knaresborough/York</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Huddersfield Line">Huddersfield Line</a> to Dewsbury/Huddersfield</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pontefract_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Pontefract Line">Pontefract Line</a> to Castleford/Pontefract/Knottingley/Goole</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Wakefield Line">Wakefield Line</a> to Wakefield/Doncaster/Sheffield</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wharfedale_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Wharfedale Line">Wharfedale Line</a> to Ilkley</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leeds-Bradford_Lines" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds-Bradford Lines">Leeds-Bradford Lines</a> to Bradford</li></ul>
